## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics and materials science
**Analysis**: The task models thermo-mechanical constitutive behavior where stress evolves with mechanical strain and temperature, capturing elastic, plastic, hyperelastic, and thermally activated material responses.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermo-elastic law: sigma = c0 * epsilon - c1 * T (stress from mechanical strain and constrained thermal expansion)
- Temperature-modulated elasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus varying linearly with temperature)
- Voce hardening law: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturating plastic strain hardening)
- Ramberg-Osgood relation: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic transition with nonlinear hardening)
- Thermal softening model: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (stress reduction due to thermally activated dislocation motion)
- Neo-Hookean hyperelasticity: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + 1) - c1 * (epsilon + 1)**(-2) (large deformation rubber-like elasticity using stretch ratio)
- Coupled damage-temperature law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 - c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T) (stiffness degradation under strain and thermal exposure)
- Power-law thermal dependence: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 / (1 + c2 * T) (steady-state flow stress modulated by temperature)
- Bilinear thermo-mechanical coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T + c2 * epsilon * T (interactive linear effects of strain and temperature)
- Modified Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 * (1 - c3 * T)**c4 (temperature-dependent plastic hardening exponent and saturation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear elastic response at small strain → Direct proportionality sigma = c * epsilon
- Elastic-plastic yield transition → Kinked derivatives, piecewise linearity, or sublinear power-law sigma ~ epsilon^p with 0 < p < 1
- Thermal stress generation → Additive independent temperature term sigma = -c * T representing constrained thermal expansion
- Large-strain hyperelasticity → Rational or inverse power terms in stretch ratio (1 + epsilon), e.g., sigma ~ (1+epsilon) - c*(1+epsilon)^-2
- Stiffness degradation / material damage → Multiplicative attenuation factor (1 - c * epsilon^n) scaling the baseline mechanical response
- Thermal softening of modulus → Temperature-dependent prefactor (c0 + c1 * T) or exponential c * exp(c1 * T) modulating strain response
- Work hardening / strain strengthening → Sublinear power-law c * epsilon^p or logarithmic c * log(1 + c * epsilon) terms dominating at higher strain
- Approaching fracture / material instability → Denominator singularity or rapid divergence as strain approaches a critical value sigma ~ c / (c_crit - epsilon)

Wait, let's look closely at the GT structure again:
`c0*epsilon**2 + c2*(T - c3)*log(epsilon + c4)`
= `c0*epsilon**2 + c2*T*log(epsilon+c4) - c2*c3*log(epsilon+c4)`
= `A * epsilon**2 + B * T * log(epsilon+1) + C * log(epsilon+1)`
where `A, B, C` are constants.
So the GT is a linear combination of `epsilon**2`, `T*log(epsilon+1)`, and `log(epsilon+1)`.
Any candidate that matches must be expressible as `k1 * epsilon**2 + k2 * T * log(epsilon+1) + k3 * log(epsilon+1)`.
Let's check candidates that have this exact structure or can simplify to it.
Many candidates have `sqrt(T)*epsilon` or `sin` or `exp`. These are linearly independent. So they must have coefficient 0.
But if a candidate has `sqrt(T)*c0*epsilon`, and `c0` is a free constant, we can set `c0=0`.
So we should look for candidates that contain `epsilon**2`, `T*log(...)`, `log(...)`, and possibly other terms that can be zeroed out.
Let's re-evaluate candidates with this in mind.

Candidate 1: `c0*log(c1*epsilon + 1) + c2*epsilon**2 + c3*exp(T*c4)*log(c5*epsilon + 1) + epsilon*(sqrt(T)*c6 + c7)`
Has `exp(T*c4)*log(...)`. Cannot match `T*log(...)`. NO MATCH.

Candidate 2: `(c0*epsilon + c1 + (T*c2 + c3)*(sqrt(T)*c4*epsilon + c5*log(c6*epsilon + 1) + c7*sin(c8*epsilon + c9)))/(T*c2 + c3)`
Simplifies to `c5*log(c6*epsilon+1) + c7*sin(...) + sqrt(T)*c4*epsilon + (c0*epsilon+c1)/(T*c2+c3)`.
No `epsilon**2`. NO MATCH.

Candidate 3: `(c0*epsilon + (T*c1 + c2)*(c3*log(c4*epsilon + 1) + c5*epsilon**2 + epsilon*(sqrt(T)*c6 + c7)))/(T*c1 + c2)`
Simplifies to `c3*log(c4*epsilon+1) + c5*epsilon**2 + epsilon*(sqrt(T)*c6+c7) + c0*epsilon/(T*c1+c2)`.
Has `epsilon**2` and `log(...)`. But has `sqrt(T)*epsilon` and `epsilon/(T...)`. Can we zero them? `c6=0, c7=0, c0=0`. Then it becomes `c3*log(c4*epsilon+1) + c5*epsilon**2`.
But GT has `T*log(...)`. This candidate has no `T` in the log term after simplification! The `T` was in the denominator `(T*c1+c2)` which canceled out. So it cannot produce `T*log(...)`. NO MATCH.

Candidate 4: `(T*c0 + c1 + (c2*epsilon + c3)*(sqrt(T)*c4*epsilon + c5*log(c6*epsilon + 1) + c7*sin(c8*epsilon + c9)))/(c2*epsilon + c3)`
Simplifies to `sqrt(T)*c4*epsilon + c5*log(...) + c7*sin(...) + (T*c0+c1)/(c2*epsilon+c3)`.
No `epsilon**2`. NO MATCH.

Candidate 5: Rational in T. NO MATCH.

Candidate 6: `(c0*epsilon + c1 + (T*c2 + c3)*(c4*log(c5*epsilon + 1) + epsilon*(sqrt(T)*c6 + c7)))/(T*c2 + c3)`
Simplifies to `c4*log(c5*epsilon+1) + epsilon*(sqrt(T)*c6+c7) + (c0*epsilon+c1)/(T*c2+c3)`.
No `epsilon**2`. NO MATCH.

Candidate 7: `c0*log(...) + c2*sin(...) + epsilon*(T*c5 + c6)`
Has `T*epsilon`. GT has no `T*epsilon`. NO MATCH.

Candidate 8: `sqrt(T)*c0*epsilon + c1*log(c2*epsilon + 1) + c3*epsilon**3 + c4*sin(c5*epsilon) + c6*epsilon`
Has `epsilon**3`. GT has `epsilon**2`. NO MATCH.

Wait, I might have missed some candidates or misread them. Let's carefully scan for `T*log(epsilon+1)` or `(T*c + d)*log(epsilon+1)`.
Actually, the GT is `c0*epsilon**2 + c2*(T - c3)*log(epsilon + c4)`.
This is `A*epsilon**2 + B*T*log(epsilon+1) + C*log(epsilon+1)`.
Let's check Candidate 14 again: `(c0*(T*c1 + 1)*log(c2*epsilon + 1) + epsilon*(c3*epsilon + (c4 + c5*epsilon)*(T*c1 + 1)))/(T*c1 + 1)`
= `c0*log(c2*epsilon+1) + epsilon*(c3*epsilon/(T*c1+1) + c4 + c5*epsilon)`
= `c0*log(...) + c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon**2 + c3*epsilon**2/(T*c1+1)`.
This has `epsilon**2/(T...)`. Not matching.

Let's check Candidate 30: `(epsilon*(c0*(T*c1 + 1)*exp(T*c2) + c3*epsilon + (c4 + c5*epsilon)*(T*c1 + 1)))/(T*c1 + 1)`
Has `exp(T)`.

Let's check Candidate 48: `(c0*epsilon**2 + (T*c1 + 1)*(sqrt(T)*c2*epsilon + c3*epsilon + c4*log(c5*epsilon + 1)))/(T*c1 + 1)`
= `c4*log(...) + sqrt(T)*c2*epsilon + c3*epsilon + c0*epsilon**2/(T*c1+1)`.
Not matching.

Let's check Candidate 54: `(T*c0 + c1 + (T*c2 + c3)*(c4*log(c5*epsilon + 1) + c6*epsilon**2 + epsilon*(sqrt(T)*c7 + c8)))/(T*c2 + c3)`
= `c4*log(...) + c6*epsilon**2 + epsilon*(sqrt(T)*c7+c8) + (T*c0+c1)/(T*c2+c3)`.
Has `sqrt(T)*epsilon`.

Wait, is there any candidate that exactly matches `c0*epsilon**2 + c1*T*log(epsilon+1) + c2*log(epsilon+1)`?
Maybe I missed one. Let's look at candidates with `(T*c1 + c2)*log(...)` in the numerator, divided by something that cancels out, or just added.
Actually, many candidates are of the form `(A + (T*c1+c2)*B)/(T*c1+c2) = B + A/(T*c1+c2)`.
If `A=0`, it simplifies to `B`.
So if a candidate is `(T*c1 + c2)*(c3*log(c4*epsilon + 1) + c5*epsilon**2) / (T*c1 + c2)`, it simplifies to `c3*log(...) + c5*epsilon**2`.
But GT has `T*log(...)`. The `T` must be inside the log coefficient.
In the form `(T*c1+c2)*B / (T*c1+c2)`, the `T` cancels out! So `B` cannot contain `T` unless it's multiplied by `(T*c1+c2)` again, which would give `T^2`.
So candidates of the form `(Num)/(Denom)` where Denom is `(T*c1+c2)` will cancel `T` from the main term. They cannot produce `T*log(...)`.
Unless the `T` is in the `A` part? `A/(T*c1+c2)` -> `T*c0/(T*c1+c2)` -> approaches constant as T->inf, but not `T*log`.
So rational forms with `(T*c1+c2)` denominator are unlikely to match `T*log(...)`.

What about candidates that are just sums?
Candidate 40: `c0*log(c1*epsilon + 1) + c2*epsilon**2 + c3*log(c4*epsilon + 1) + epsilon*(sqrt(T)*c5 + c6)`
If `c5=0, c6=0`, it's `c0*log(...) + c2*epsilon**2 + c3*log(...)`. No `T`.

Candidate 81: `c0*exp(T*c1)*log(c2*epsilon + 1) + ...` -> `exp(T)`.

If `c1=1`, `T**c1 = T`. So `T*c2*log(c3*epsilon+1)`. This matches `T*log(...)`!
Let's check Candidate 77 carefully:
`T*c0*epsilon + T**c1*c2*log(c3*epsilon + 1) + c4*epsilon**3 + c5*epsilon`
GT: `c0*epsilon**2 + c2*(T - c3)*log(epsilon + c4)` = `A*epsilon**2 + B*T*log(epsilon+1) + C*log(epsilon+1)`.
Candidate 77 has `T*c0*epsilon`. GT has no `T*epsilon`. Can we set `c0=0`? Yes.
Then it becomes `T**c1*c2*log(c3*epsilon + 1) + c4*epsilon**3 + c5*epsilon`.
GT has `epsilon**2`. Candidate 77 has `epsilon**3`. Can `epsilon**3` match `epsilon**2`? No, linearly independent.
So Candidate 77 is NO MATCH.

3. Have `sqrt(T)*epsilon` which is linearly independent from `epsilon**2` and `log(epsilon+1)`.

To determine which candidates match the Ground Truth (GT), we first analyze the mathematical structure of the GT:
`GT = c0*epsilon**2 + c2*(T - c3)*log(epsilon + c4)`
Expanding the second term gives:
`GT = c0*epsilon**2 + c2*T*log(epsilon + c4) - c2*c3*log(epsilon + c4)`
This shows the GT is a linear combination of three linearly independent basis functions:
1. `epsilon**2`
2. `T * log(epsilon + 1)` (since `c4 = 1`)
3. `log(epsilon + 1)`

Any valid candidate must be algebraically reducible to exactly this form (allowing free constants to be set to zero or adjusted). We evaluate each candidate against this requirement:

- **Rational Forms (e.g., Candidates 2, 3, 4, 6, 9, 11, 12, 13, 14, 26, 28, 36, 37, 38, 48, 50, 51, 52, 53, 54, 60, 61, 62, 63, 65, 76, 82, 83):** Many candidates use a structure like `(A + (T*c1 + c2)*B) / (T*c1 + c2)`. This simplifies to `B + A/(T*c1 + c2)`. Crucially, the `T` in the denominator cancels the `T` in the numerator's multiplier, meaning the `T` dependence is **removed** from the main term `B`. Thus, these candidates cannot produce the required `T * log(epsilon + 1)` term. Others have `T` in the numerator but not multiplying the log term, or introduce `sqrt(T)*epsilon`, `sin`, or `exp` terms that are linearly independent from the GT basis.
- **Exponential/Trigonometric `T` dependence (e.g., Candidates 1, 7, 15, 17, 18, 19, 20, 21, 23, 25, 31, 32, 33, 34, 35, 39, 41, 42, 43, 44, 45, 46, 47, 49, 55, 56, 57, 59, 64, 66, 67, 68, 69, 70, 71, 72, 73, 74, 75, 78, 79, 80, 81):** These candidates attach `T` to `exp()`, `sin()`, `cos()`, `sqrt(T)*epsilon`, or `T*epsilon`. Since `exp(T)`, `sin(T)`, `sqrt(T)*epsilon`, and `T*epsilon` are linearly independent from `T*log(epsilon+1)`, they cannot match the GT. Setting their coefficients to zero eliminates the `T` dependence entirely, leaving only `log(epsilon+1)` and `epsilon**2`, which fails to match the `T*log` term.
- **Power `T` dependence (Candidate 77):** `T**c1*c2*log(c3*epsilon + 1) + ...` If `c1=1`, this yields `T*log(...)`, but the candidate completely lacks an `epsilon**2` term (only `epsilon**3` and `epsilon` are present, which are linearly independent and cannot be transformed into `epsilon**2`). Thus, it misses a required basis function.
- **Pure Sums (e.g., Candidates 5, 8, 10, 16, 22, 24, 27, 29, 30, 40, 58, 60):** These either lack `T` in the log term, attach `T` to the wrong basis function (e.g., `T*epsilon**2` in Candidate 45), or contain irreconcilable extra terms like `exp(epsilon)`, `sin(epsilon)`, or `epsilon**3`.

After rigorous algebraic simplification and basis function comparison, **no candidate** can be made exactly equivalent to the Ground Truth across the continuous domain.
